Subject: [PLUG] trouble with php and apache2 on Debian etch
Message-ID: <47F2BB01.2070806@frankhunt.com>

Testing out my new web server and ran into this issue.  When attempting 
to run php scripts from the browser I get the option to either open the 
file with an editor or save it to disk.  Obviously, neither of these 
runs the script.  I'm running Debian etch 4.0 with apache 2.2.3 viewing 
with iceweasel 2.0.0.13.  There must be a configuration error someplace 
and I need some help.

-frank

Do you have this line in your httpd.conf


  #AddHandler cgi-script .cgi
    AddType application/x-httpd-php .php
    AddType application/x-httpd-php-source .phps

From: sandy at herring.org (Sandy Herring)

Message-ID: <20080402000316.GA3146@pickled.herring.org>

Circa 16:37:32 on Tue, 01 Apr 2008, Frank Hunt wrote: 
> drew wymore wrote:
> > On Tue, Apr 1, 2008 at 3:45 PM, Frank Hunt <linux at frankhunt.com> wrote:
[...]
> > Frank,
> > Do you have this line in your httpd.conf
> >
> >
> >   #AddHandler cgi-script .cgi
> >     AddType application/x-httpd-php .php
> >     AddType application/x-httpd-php-source .phps
> > _______________________________________________
> > PLUG mailing list
> > PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> > http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
> >
> >   
> Yes, both lines are in there.

I can't speak for Debian, but CentOS loads PHP as a Dynamic Shared
Object. If Debian statically links php, it should show up in `httpd -l'
in the compiled in modules. If not, do you have LoadModule and
AddModules lines in your httpd.conf file? e.g.

LoadModule unique_id_module   libexec/mod_unique_id.so
LoadModule setenvif_module    libexec/mod_setenvif.so
LoadModule php5_module        libexec/libphp5.so
<IfDefine SSL>
LoadModule ssl_module         libexec/libssl.so
</IfDefine>
LoadModule gzip_module        libexec/mod_gzip.so
[...]
AddModule mod_unique_id.c
AddModule mod_so.c
AddModule mod_setenvif.c
AddModule mod_php5.c
<IfDefine SSL>
AddModule mod_ssl.c
</IfDefine>
AddModule mod_gzip.c

Note that I've included more than what's needed for libphp5.so since the
order is important.

Sandy

From creswick at gmail.com  Tue Apr  1 17:30:06 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Tue, 1 Apr 2008 17:30:06 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] trouble with php and apache2 on Debian etch
In-Reply-To: <20080402000316.GA3146@pickled.herring.org>
References: <47F2BB01.2070806@frankhunt.com>
	<e2aeccd60804011611g484a35acl51aae54536beb3eb@mail.gmail.com>
	<47F2C73C.1050301@frankhunt.com>
	<20080402000316.GA3146@pickled.herring.org>
Message-ID: <c834ec80804011730w4129db3bm9d3726f17a9434be@mail.gmail.com>

On Tue, Apr 1, 2008 at 5:03 PM, Sandy Herring <sandy at herring.org> wrote:
>
>  in the compiled in modules. If not, do you have LoadModule and
>  AddModules lines in your httpd.conf file? e.g.
>
>  LoadModule unique_id_module   libexec/mod_unique_id.so
>  LoadModule setenvif_module    libexec/mod_setenvif.so
>  LoadModule php5_module        libexec/libphp5.so

I think the debian equivalent of this is the set of symbolic links in
/etc/apache2/mods-enabled

You can add/remove modules with a2enmod and a2dismod (they are in
/usr/sbin), eg:

a2enmod php5

It's worth checking, for sure -- I had the same problem about 2 months
back, but I didn't take notes.  This is one of the things I did in the
process of getting it to work though, so that may help. (I think I was
having conflicting php modules/versions, but don't quote me on that.)

--Rogan

On Tue, Apr 01, 2008 at 05:30:06PM -0700, Rogan Creswick wrote:
> I think the debian equivalent of this is the set of symbolic links in
> /etc/apache2/mods-enabled
> 
> You can add/remove modules with a2enmod and a2dismod (they are in
> /usr/sbin), eg:
> 
> a2enmod php5

Alternatively you can get a directory listing of /etc/apache2/mods-enabled and
if php5.conf and php5.load aren't there create the symlinks.  The files will
be found in /etc/apache2/mods-available

From iconoklastic at yahoo.com  Wed Apr  2 10:32:20 2008
From: iconoklastic at yahoo.com (Robert Kopp)
Date: Wed, 2 Apr 2008 10:32:20 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] ZoneMinder
Message-ID: <558937.9986.qm@web50603.mail.re2.yahoo.com>

This is a Web-based application to control video-capture devices, and seems a little tricky to set up. I am attempting to use it with SuSE 10.3.

I have Apache2, MySQL, and ZM daemons all running, and the Web interface opens at http://localhost/zm. However, I'm having trouble getting the capture devices to work. One of them is a bttv-based TV tuner. It shows a caption and the kind of random visual effects of a tuner that is not adjusted for a particular station. The other, a Phillips-based Webcam, flickers from time to time but does not display an image. (That Webcam, however, has kernel support, because it works with Ekiga.)

Has anyone else experienced such a problem, and if so, have they successfully solved it? This seems like a very worthwhile application, if it can be made to work properly.


Robert "Tim" Kopp
http://analytic.tripod.com/

I'm *sure* the fix isn't that hard -- and I really wish I could tell
you exacatly what it is, but since I can't here are some more
questions to try and jog my memory / your googleage.

Do you have multiple versions of php installed? (try removing php4, if
you have it and php5 installed)

Try reconfiguring apache/package X where X is something php/apache
related that you installed recently. (use dpkg --reconfigure
<package>).  Some of the installers, such as certain versions of
phppgadmin don't properly order the installation of their
dependencies.  If you apt-get phppgadmin without having apache
installed already, you stand a good chance of seeing this problem.
(disclaimer: this *might* be something I only ran into on an ubuntu
box... I'm not certain.)

What shows up in the apache logs when you try to load a php generated
page? (anything other than a standard file fetch? any errors about
php?)

How many php scripts have you tried this with? (It *might* be
application-local, and if your only test case was phppgadmin, maybe it
will work with something else..)

Based on old email logs of mine, it looks like I had this problem once
because only php5-common was installed, and I needed to aptitude get
php5 and some others (php5-mysql, but I don't think that was really
necessary for the downloading issue).

I hope none of those send you off on a wild goose chase.

--Rogan

It turned out to be rather trivial: "Color Palette" had to be set to YUV420P, instead of RGB or Grey, which I would have considered more likely. I don't know whether this is generally true for Phillips Webcams.

Robert Kopp <iconoklastic at yahoo.com> wrote: This is a Web-based application to control video-capture devices, and seems a little tricky to set up. I am attempting to use it with SuSE 10.3.

I have Apache2, MySQL, and ZM daemons all running, and the Web interface opens at http://localhost/zm. However, I'm having trouble getting the capture devices to work. One of them is a bttv-based TV tuner. It shows a caption and the kind of random visual effects of a tuner that is not adjusted for a particular station. The other, a Phillips-based Webcam, flickers from time to time but does not display an image. (That Webcam, however, has kernel support, because it works with Ekiga.)

Has anyone else experienced such a problem, and if so, have they successfully solved it? This seems like a very worthwhile application, if it can be made to work properly.

Frank Hunt wrote:
> <stuff deleted>
>
> Just as an FYI, the phpinfo.php and other scripts work from the command 
> line.  Just not from apache.
>
>   
Silly question but one that bites me all the time, are the .php scripts 
executable by the Apache user (User in the httpd.conf file).  Also, from 
my experience with Apache/PHP/Perl/etc, do not depend on the 
distributions packaging of Apache, it is usually broken wrt PHP, and 
other modules you might need are missing (web dav and dav fs).  Build 
Apache from source and point the configure script to php etc with 
--with-php=/path/to/php/dev.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Thu Apr  3 09:57:25 2008
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Thu, 3 Apr 2008 09:57:25 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] trouble with php and apache2 on Debian etch
In-Reply-To: <47F4E417.90407@comcast.net>
References: <47F2BB01.2070806@frankhunt.com> <47F400CA.4040000@frankhunt.com>
	<47F4E417.90407@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <200804030957.25429.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Michael Ewan
# on Thursday 03 April 2008 07:05:

>Also, from
>my experience with Apache/PHP/Perl/etc, do not depend on the
>distributions packaging of Apache, it is usually broken wrt PHP, and
>other modules you might need are missing (web dav and dav fs).

I highly doubt that this is the case with debian.  At most, you would 
need to install the appropriate package, which will typically configure 
itself.  If that fails, read the directions.

Googling the error "exec format failed" implies that you're trying to 
run it as a cgi without a shebang, which means your mod_php isn't 
catching it.

If you're using httpd.conf and not apache2.conf, that might be part of 
the problem.

  /usr/share/doc/apache2.2-common/README.Debian

--Eric

Wow thats a lot of money. This Laptop should be compatible with:

Ultumix, Ubuntu, Linux Mint, and other Debian based Distros. It may also work with some RPM based distros. 

You will most likely need to remove the internal wireless card and install a GNU/Linux compatible one. I would recommend an ASUS PCMCIA card I like but you probably have PCI Express. I would go with USB.

information about the design of the device.

On 04 Apr 2008 19:37:08 -0700
Russell Senior <seniorr at aracnet.com> dijo:

> Russell> If it's an Intel card, which is reasonably likely, it should
> Russell> work okay.  Intel is actively working on the driver.
> 
> Google and HP say it is the Intel Pro/Wireless 4965AGN radio.  I don't
> have one, but I believe that should be working now.

Not exactly working. I have the Intel 4965agn in my Thinkpad with Gutsy
x86_64. The wireless connects reasonably well if you have a strong
signal. But then it just hangs up on you at random. The fix is to
upgrade your kernel or, as I decided to do, put up with it until Hardy
comes out. Hardy comes with a kernel that makes it work. 

I understand 64-bit Windows also has similar problems with the 4965agn. 

If yours won't arrive for a couple of weeks yet, Hardy Final may be out
by the time it gets here.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Apr  5 09:13:24 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 5 Apr 2008 09:13:24 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Linux Webcams
In-Reply-To: <47F6C363.5090509@verizon.net>
References: <32699.198.182.194.170.1207348661.squirrel@clueserver.org>
	<47F6C363.5090509@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <20080405161324.GB24510@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Fri, Apr 04, 2008 at 05:10:11PM -0700, Bruce KIlpatrick wrote:
> Alan,
> 
> If yours has a webcam and you get it working, I would be interested in 
> knowing how you did it.  I haven't had any luck with mine.  I keep 
> trying to make it to a FreeGeek clinic, but haven't made it yet.  I am 
> running Gutsy AMD 64.

If you come to the clinic with this issue, please do a bit of homework
first.  Look at your laptop on http://www.linux-laptop.net/ .  Do an
"lspci" as root and find out what model of camera you have, then Google
for that device number and Linux. Check the Ubuntu Forums.  And read
the pointers for this article: http://snurl.com/23jv7 (inquirer news
2007/04/30 article on USB cameras).  That is what we would start out
by doing, and if you come in with some of this knowledge we are more
likely to solve the problem in the time available.

Keith

Subject: [PLUG] Gutsy Intel wifi
In-Reply-To: <20080404210305.805b1219.johnxj@comcast.net>

John Jason Jordan wrote:
> Not exactly working. I have the Intel 4965agn in my Thinkpad with Gutsy
> x86_64. The wireless connects reasonably well if you have a strong
> signal. But then it just hangs up on you at random. The fix is to
> upgrade your kernel or, as I decided to do, put up with it until Hardy
> comes out. Hardy comes with a kernel that makes it work. 

<topic swipe>

I have a T61 running 32-bit Gutsy and a 3945ABG.  It became less-stable when I
upgraded from Feisty to Gutsy crashing 1-4 times per day requiring a reboot
(most times a hard power off).  It installs by default using the ipw3945 module
which is now deprecated by Intel in favor of the iwlwifi system.

Here's what I did to use the latest version of iwlwifi (from memory):

aptitude install linux-source
cd /usr/src
tar jxf linux-source-2.6.22.tar.bz2

cd /lib/modules
rsync -axHP 2.6.22-14-generic/ 2.6.22-14-generic.bak/
rsync -axHP /lib/firmware/ /lib/firmware.bak/
cd 2.6.22-14-generic
ln -s /usr/src/linux-source-2.6.22 source
cp /boot/config-2.6.22-14-generic source/.config.old
cd source
make oldconfig

cd /usr/src
wget http://intellinuxwireless.org/iwlwifi/downloads/iwlwifi-1.2.25.tgz

wget \
http://intellinuxwireless.org/iwlwifi/downloads/iwlwifi-3945-ucode-2.14.1.5.tgz

tar zxf iwlwifi-3945-ucode-2.14.1.5.tgz
tar zxf iwlwifi-1.2.25.tgz

cp iwlwifi-3945-ucode-2.14.1.5/iwlwifi-3945-1.ucode \
/lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic/

chmod 644 /lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic/iwlwifi-3945-1.ucode

cd iwlwifi-1.2.25
make
sudo make install

rm \
/lib/modules/2.6.22-14-generic/ubuntu/wireless/iwlwifi/iwlwifi/origin/iwl3945.ko

* Append to /etc/modprobe.d/blacklist
-----START-----
# 2008-04-05, krisa, block ipw3945 in favor of iwlwifi
blacklist ipw3945
blacklist ieee80211
blacklist ieee80211_crypt
-----END-----

* Append to /etc/modules
-----START-----
# 2008-04-05, iwlwifi (new Intel wifi driver)
iwlwifi_mac80211
iwl3945
-----END-----

* Reboot


Take note that I did this, well, early today; I am still testing.  So far my
laptop has been up for 20 hours, with one move 20 miles from home to office
(where I am now).  Network at home is open, and office WPA.  So far so good.

krisa at kavula(~)$ uptime
 21:53:46 up 20:14,  2 users,  load average: 0.10, 0.12, 0.09

-- 
I'm just a packet pusher.

On Sun, 6 Apr 2008 18:20:02 -0700
"William Milmoe" <wmilmoe at gmail.com> dijo:

> I am a non technical person using  a compaq Armada E500 with 256k memory and
> Ubuntu Gutsy G.  I joined this list in Jan? 2008, to hopefully learn by
> osmosis but not sure I have absorbed much yet.
> 
> I would like to be able to record radio talk shows for later listening and
> youtube videos for off-line viewing.

Bill,

Gutsy comes with Sound Recorder, which should be able to record the
radio talk shows. I've never used it, however, so I don't know how easy
it would be to set it up to do so unattended. 

Regarding youtube, I am not aware of any way to record them. In the
past I poked around a couple times trying to figure out how to save a
youtube video, but never found out how. Having said that, with only 256
Mb (I'm sure you meant Mb, not Kb), you might find recording video to
be a problem. Your RAM is barely enough to run Gutsy, and I'm sure
you've seen your computer using the swap file. The problem is that the
swap is painfully slow compared to RAM, and it may not work fast enough
to process the video.

Quanta Plus (part of KDE) is the most WYSIWIG I've seen among the free 
tools. Komodo will run on Linux but is non-free. I use Komodo for Ruby 
and Perl development but not for web pages.

In general, a lot depends on what your web pages have to do to earn 
their keep. If you're building something like Ruby on Rails web 
applications, I'd recommend investing in a good overall IDE, like Komodo.

On Sun, 6 Apr 2008, Alex wrote:

> In short I need a Linux compatible tool which would allow me to do HTML
> page layout, without digging through HTML tags, and possibly support CSS.
> I don't mind if someone advises on any commercial Linux compatible HTML
> editing tool.

Alex,

   I suggest that you think more about what you want to do. HTML was always
supposed to be used for content, but its role was hijacked for layout, too.
Layout should be separate from content. Use CSS for layout, and by changing
that file you can alter appearance without touching the .html context. Look
at the W3C web site to learn the few differences between html and xhtml, and
how to design your web site to be compliant with those standards.

   If you're going to learn you might as well learn how it should be done.
Also, by using any text editor of your choice to write the html and css
files you can see how they look on various web browsers (firefox, opera,
lynx, etc.). I doubt that a GUI developer shows you the differences.

Rich

There is 'youtube-dl': http://www.arrakis.es/~rggi3/youtube-dl/
It's a command-line app, but it's simple enough to use:

  youtube-dl http:<YOUR_YOUTUBE_URL_HERE> -o amazing_video.flv

It seems to break every six months or so (changes on the YouTube side
of things, presumably), but the author quickly updates the software
and all is well again.

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Mon Apr  7 07:29:15 2008
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Mon, 7 Apr 2008 08:29:15 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] Any good Linux compatible WYSIWYG HTML editor
In-Reply-To: <20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <47F996BC.205@mailswamp.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804070606190.790@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <18426.12219.118624.770875@localhost.localdomain>

John Jason Jordan writes:
 > On Mon, 7 Apr 2008 06:11:35 -0700 (PDT)
 > Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> dijo:
 > 
 > > Layout should be separate from content. 
 > 
 > At the risk of hijacking this thread, why?
 > _______________________________________________
 > PLUG mailing list
 > PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
 > http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

Maintainability, readability.  It also reduces the number of bytes a
website user has to pull per page request.  An external CSS file gets
loaded once per browser session.  And a web page built on the CSS
principle is much shorter than one using tables for layout.  Another
reason: it is easier to render the content differently accoring to
media type (handheld, browser, printer) using CSS, since it has
built-in support for @media types.  Say goodbye to the "printer
friendly page" button.  Just print and let CSS work its magic
(provided you defined a set of styles for @media printer).  Every page
now has a printer friendly version lurking.

You could take it a step further and send XML to the browser, with a
reference to an XSLT stylesheet to digest the data in the XML document
and render it as HTML, which itself pulls in a CSS stylesheet for the
actual browser formatting.  But that might be overkill.  And XSLT is
not exactly terse.

All this talk about separation of content and style brings up another
idea for the whizzywig coveters: a CMS system.
--
Carlos Konstanski

From sjansen at buscaluz.org  Mon Apr  7 07:39:08 2008
From: sjansen at buscaluz.org (Stuart Jansen)
Date: Mon, 07 Apr 2008 08:39:08 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] semantic markup and CSS (was: Any good Linux
	compatible	WYSIWYG HTML editor)
In-Reply-To: <20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <47F996BC.205@mailswamp.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804070606190.790@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <1207579148.13855.17.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>


On Mon, 2008-04-07 at 07:08 -0700, John Jason Jordan wrote:
> On Mon, 7 Apr 2008 06:11:35 -0700 (PDT)
> Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> dijo:
> 
> > Layout should be separate from content. 
> 
> At the risk of hijacking this thread, why?

Well, that depends.

If you're throwing together a couple pages to share pictures of your cat
with friends, don't bother. Go ahead, use every dirty trick in the book
to get the job done quickly and move on with life.

If you're creating a small site (< 20 pages) to advertise your
on-the-side consulting business, there are several advantages to
semantic markup and CSS. One is that it tends to result in higher Google
rankings. Another is that it tends to be more future proof, so long as
you resist the urge to indulge in too many hacks for IE (or keep them in
a separate stylesheet). In other words, it tends to work better as more
standards compliant browsers are released and viewers increasingly moves
from computer screens to cell phones and other devices.

If you're a medium sized business with hundreds or thousands of pages,
separation of content and design makes it _much_ easier to rebrand you
site without rewriting all those pages.  To be honest, unless you're a
Web designer, a hobbyist that likes to tinker with CSS, or a company
trying to find success through rebranding, the ability to restyle your
entire site probably isn't a big sell. But for some people it is.

If you're a programmers, separating content and design is like building
good modular code according to a recognized style guide. Sure your code
might work even if it isn't well implemented, but 3 years from now as
you suffer trying to add "just one more feature" you'll wish you'd taken
the time to do things right.

If you're a neat freaks like me, mixing content and design is like
hiding dirty socks under your bed. Sure no one else will ever know or
care, but it'll drive you crazy 'cause it just ain't right.

From michael at jamhome.us  Mon Apr  7 09:17:51 2008
From: michael at jamhome.us (Michael)
Date: Mon, 7 Apr 2008 09:17:51 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Any good Linux compatible WYSIWYG HTML editor why
 separate layout/content
In-Reply-To: <20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <47F996BC.205@mailswamp.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804070606190.790@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <28289.170.135.241.46.1207585071.squirrel@mail.jamhome.us>


John Jason Jordan wrote:
>> Layout should be separate from content.
>
> At the risk of hijacking this thread, why?

Consider four visitors to your web space:

 Renee on her new iPhone
 Cal with his text only browser
 Michael viewing it on a computer display
 John printing a copy to read offline

All of those want to see your content.  All of their displays have different
requirements for how layout will optimally fit the presentation space. If you
tightly bind the layout and content you have to redo your entire web space for
each of the target displays.

On another level the powers that be are finicky about how their pages dislay
and are prone to making changes to freshen up the appearance for the style du
jour.  Best to have the content separate so you can just update the layout.

For how well this can work in real life see the examples at:
http://www.csszengarden.com/

     Michael Rasmussen
 Be Appropriate && Follow Your Curiosity

On Mon, 7 Apr 2008 07:27:21 -0700
Aaron <ke7ezt at gmail.com> dijo:

> Totally agree with you Richard.  Learning the fundamentals will give him
> better results in the long run.

Thanks for the clarifications, I think.

In my case I would have to become extremely hungry to become a web
designer. I will never design more than a simple little site like the
IPA site that I recently created, using its GUI:

http://www.ipa4linguists.com

I don't know anything about CSS, but when I see the word "style" I
grasp the idea - that is, assuming there is some parallel in meaning to
styles as used in word processors. I have been using styles in word
processors since they first appeared.

My problem is that I am accustomed to applying the formatting (styles)
*as I produce the content*. It seems a total waste of time to just
create the content willy-nilly and then have to go all the way back
through it to do the formatting and design. In a sense, when I create a
paper document I create a "CSS" before I start, then tag the various
parts with the styles as I go along. In fact, the design factors even
determine to some extent the content. Should I start this topic on this
page? Will it fit? Or should I put it in a sidebar? Should I use a
pull-quote? If so, where would be a good place to put it? 

Therefore, design and content are part of the same process to me.
Separating them might make sense if you are a newspaper with dozens of
writers producing articles - then you need someone to put it all
together at the end. But when I am doing everything myself, it's much
more efficient to do it all at once.

But maybe I misunderstood the meanings of "content" and "layout."

John Jason Jordan wrote:
> I don't know anything about CSS, but when I see the word "style" I
> grasp the idea - that is, assuming there is some parallel in meaning to
> styles as used in word processors. I have been using styles in word
> processors since they first appeared.

There is a huge parallel.  And you understand how being able to redefine the
style and having the change apply all through the document is a great saver of
effort while ensuring the change is applied correctly and consistantly.

> My problem is that I am accustomed to applying the formatting (styles)
> *as I produce the content*. It seems a total waste of time to just
> create the content willy-nilly and then have to go all the way back
> through it to do the formatting and design.

Yeah, so?  Do the styles first and fill in the content.  Or iterate and change
styles as the content shows issues with your original decisions.  That's a
workflow issue, not a content/layout separation issue.

variants of Linux on them with minimal fuss.  Recently, my ASUS

carpet).  I replaced it with another ASUS (AMD based) with onboard 
video/lan/sound and CentOS picked it all up beautifully on install.

On Mon, 7 Apr 2008, Alex wrote:

> However, the the person with whom I'm developing a new site, doesn't know
> a thing about HTML/XHTML or CSS. He is a great artist but not technically
> inclined. Therefore, I'm trying to find a graphical tool which would allow
> him at least to create a basic site layout and all that eye candy. So I
> can code it up and make it working within existing CGI::Application
> framework.

Alex,

   Well, why not do what I did when I re-wrote our web site several years
ago? Search with Google for web site templates, find one he likes, download
the .css files and salt to taste.

   Looking at the examples is the quickest and best way to see what's
possible. I actually combined two samples into the design I wanted, but he
may find someting exactly to his liking.

   The nice thing about this approach is the speed with which the site can be
created and tweaked. No need to start from scratch. Also, the two Eric Meyer
books on CSS were -- and continue to be -- exceptionally helpful for
designing menus, creating a printer version .css, and other useful ideas.

Rich

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804071034120.790@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Mon, 7 Apr 2008, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> I don't know anything about CSS, but when I see the word "style" I grasp
> the idea - that is, assuming there is some parallel in meaning to styles
> as used in word processors. I have been using styles in word processors
> since they first appeared.

> My problem is that I am accustomed to applying the formatting (styles)
> *as I produce the content*. It seems a total waste of time to just
> create the content willy-nilly and then have to go all the way back
> through it to do the formatting and design.

   Which is exactly why you want semantic markup and to separate the styles
completely. That's the advantage of separating the styles (.css) from the
content (.xhtml) for web sites, and one of the advantages of separating the
styles (.sty) from the content (.tex) when writing in LaTeX.

   Rather than willy-nillying your processed words, John, you focus on
content and make sure you are clearly and effectively communicting. Then you
apply the style that you want, because that's already prepared in a separate
template file.

   By the way, there are specific style templates (i.e., package) for
typesetting linguistic papers with LaTeX. They also work with the GUI front
end called LyX.

   Futzing with styles in a complex document using a word processor turns out
results of the same visual and nutritive quality as processed cheese. This
is one reason many universities have their own LaTeX thesis classes: they
determine the style they want for all submitted theses and dissertations,
then each student creates the individual content.

   However, ...

Rich

I know this is awfully close to taboo, but is there any chance he
could run Visio? I have yet to find a comparable Linux compatible tool
for creating mockups, but Inkscape *might* be a viable alternative,
depending on how much effort/structure he wants.  At my office, we do
almost all of our UI design in Visio, regardless of what it will end
up being implemented with. No other tool I've found offers the same
combination of flexibility and reusable components (buttons,
scrollbars, etc.).

Would not text-only compatibility be easily implementable with the CSS
paradigm we're pushing?  Lynx would simply ignore the styles, and all
that's left is the content (and [lack of] javascript; here is where
you would have to spend compatibility efforts).

An actual place I've used text/plain HTTP responses is in web actions
that are designed to be called from cron, and their output parsed by
another program.  I call it poorman's SOA.

From bsr at spek.org  Mon Apr  7 12:52:34 2008

 separate layout/content
In-Reply-To: <18426.28006.360219.656959@localhost.localdomain>
References: <47F996BC.205@mailswamp.com>	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804070606190.790@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>	<20080407070850.489d8d0f.johnxj@comcast.net>	<28289.170.135.241.46.1207585071.squirrel@mail.jamhome.us>	<47FA6480.2090902@spek.org>	<29757.170.135.241.46.1207593360.squirrel@mail.jamhome.us>

Carlos Konstanski wrote:
> Would not text-only compatibility be easily implementable with the CSS
> paradigm we're pushing?  Lynx would simply ignore the styles, and all
> that's left is the content (and [lack of] javascript; here is where
> you would have to spend compatibility efforts).

Mostly, yes, but not entirely; how your content is ordered in the source 
matters to users using browsers like lynx, it doesn't matter to users 
using a regular gui browser.

> An actual place I've used text/plain HTTP responses is in web actions
> that are designed to be called from cron, and their output parsed by
> another program.  I call it poorman's SOA.

That sounds like an API and not a web site.. and a XML or JSON response 
is (usually) just text too, content type headers are set to be pleasant 
and to indicate what the content which follows might be for clients that 
care.

--Brent

> 
>    Which is exactly why you want semantic markup and to separate the styles
> completely. That's the advantage of separating the styles (.css) from the
> content (.xhtml) for web sites, and one of the advantages of separating the
> styles (.sty) from the content (.tex) when writing in LaTeX.
> 
>    Rather than willy-nillying your processed words, John, you focus on
> content and make sure you are clearly and effectively communicting. Then you
> apply the style that you want, because that's already prepared in a separate

> typesetting linguistic papers with LaTeX. They also work with the GUI front
> end called LyX.
> 
>    Futzing with styles in a complex document using a word processor turns out
> results of the same visual and nutritive quality as processed cheese. This
> is one reason many universities have their own LaTeX thesis classes: they
> determine the style they want for all submitted theses and dissertations,

Hmmm ... speaking of LyX:

1. LyX will save to HTML -- you ought to be able to do a static web page 
  with it.

2. The LyX/R integration on "literate" documents is near perfect now. 
You can edit a document in LyX with embedded R code to generate the 
graphs, for example. It might not be much of a stretch to embed a 
scripting language like Python in a LyX page and make dynamic web sites 
with LyX.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Apr  8 08:30:55 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 8 Apr 2008 08:30:55 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Thinkpad help: On the topic of my stupid laptop (Keith?)
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804071315080.11158@shadow.bitmine.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804071315080.11158@shadow.bitmine.net>
Message-ID: <20080408153055.GA5356@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Mon, Apr 07, 2008 at 01:23:11PM -0500, Jeme A Brelin wrote:
> 
> I recently acquired an advanced minidock for my Thinkapd T61.  I dropped 
> the laptop in and the USB ports fired up and did the right thing.  The 
> external hard drive kicked in and mounted.  All seemed good.
> 
> Until...
> 
> 1)
> I plugged in the external audio connector for my desktop stereo system and 
> found that it didn't work... only the onboard speakers worked.  Subsequent 
> testing showed that even headphones in the port on the laptop do not work. 
> The onboard spekaers are not muted and the headphones do not play sound.

While I don't have a T61, I suspect all three issues stem from the recent
migration of Linux and/or Gnome to "Hardware Abstraction Layer".   The
audio connection may be something as simple as gain control, and the 
GUI you are using should have an applet that communicates the gain setting
through the HAL.  

Note that headphones, and PC external speakers,  have impedances of around 
200 ohms while consumer audio equipment inputs have impedances of about
10K ohms.  Studio audio equipment is typically 600 ohms impedance. I can
imagine some Chinese engineer that doesn't understand this, designing
a headphone amplifier that doesn't work right with higher impedance than
cheap headphones.  However, it is also possible to cut down the output
gain from the laptop and increase the gain of the audio equipment and
avoid clipping and distortion.  So the first trick is to get the headphone
output port working right with with some cheap headphones, then move on
to the external equipment.


> 2)
> Undocking didn't work.  Now, I should let y'all know right now that I 
> (perhaps stupidly) removed the partition that had all those Thinkpad 
> utilities and this blue ThinkVantage button is apparently useless. 
> Pressing the undock button made the little green triangle flash a bit, but 
> the second button was still it with a big red NO sign.  I had to shut down 
> the machine to get the undock to work properly.
> 
> Resolutions?  IBM wants huge money for a restore CD that will put the 
> partition back in place.  I should have made one, I know.  Too late.  Shut 
> up... but help me, anyway.

Personally, I order laptops with the smallest hard drive available.  After
verifying that the machine begins to boot, but before seeing any EULA 
screens, I shut down and store the original drive in a safe place.  Then I
put in a different large hard drive and install Linux on that.   Thus, I
have two unused T31 boot drives, one with WinXP and one with Win2K, waiting 
n a shelf for the day I decide to reverse-compile them ("EULA?  I didn't
agree to no stinking EULA!  If you don't want the bits examined, don't
put them on my hardware!")

Not that that does you any good, but other folks are buying T61s and 
perhaps one of them will do the same, and perhaps a copy of the hard
drive bits can be made available to you.

That said - undocking in Linux is also managed by the HAL ... badly.
If you are using gnome, the information filters through the applet
"Power Manager" (written by Ritchie Hughes in the UK).  Like everything
involved in power in HAL, it takes a while for it to detect AC adapter
changes, lid closure, etc.   Perhaps 10 seconds.  If I unplug my T31
from the minidock, I have to wait about 10 seconds before closing it
and sticking it in the backpack.  I also remember having to fiddle 
with some of the Power Manager settings to make it work approximately
right (I forget which settings).  

> 3)
> The external video did nothing.  I have a Samsung 213TW LCD on the DVI 
> output and it has the same native resolution as the 15.4" WXGA display on 
> the laptop.  Can I get them both working with xinerama behavior?  If not, 
> can I get a mirrored display?  And if not, can I at least get the LCD to 
> work at all via the minidock?

HAL again.  Dammit.  With pre-HAL distros, my T31 would do the right
thing, recognizing external monitors and projectors when they were plugged
in during operation.  Now I need to reboot for the T31 to recognize the
external video connections.  I am told that this is fixed in the bleeding
edge kernels and Xorg servers, but I haven't tried those myself.  For
now, try rebooting with the monitor attached.  Also, use LSPCI and look
at /var/log/Xorg.0.log to see what hardware you are running, and look at
the results when booting with and without the external hardware.

- - - - - - - - - -

In general, I suggest trying these things out with a variety of Live CDs
of various ages.  The newest thing you can get your hands on, and some 2
and 4 year old stuff.  That is a relatively quick way of identifying
incompatabilities.  Most of it seems to be HAL.

Also, look at the linux-laptop.net website, the thinkwiki.org website,
and see if there is a version of "tpctl" or Thinkpad Control that works
with the T61.  

After the rest of you get the T61 debugged, I might buy one :-)

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

Hello Richard,
Thanks to you and every one else for the posted hints or suggestions.
However, you know those pesky artists.
They would never accept some one else's piece of work to be included into their 
creation. So, using pre-programmed HTML templates is out of the picture.
My artistic friend thinks in terms of shapes, colors and its combinations.
He wants to play freely with web page objects changing their colors, shapes and 
combinations without thinking about underlying HTML/XHTML tags and CSS 
formatting directives.
He gave me an example of Photoshop or GIMP, where you're actually creating a 
piece of art without thinking about what is going on under the hood.
The same kind of tool he would like to have for the web design as well.
I must admit, that there is a truth to these words.

Alex

> designing menus, creating a printer version .css, and other useful ideas.

> Rich

From johnxj at comcast.net  Wed Apr  9 12:10:37 2008
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Wed, 9 Apr 2008 12:10:37 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless (sigh)
Message-ID: <20080409121037.77d464bf.johnxj@comcast.net>

Now I've done it. The Intel 4965agn in my Thinkpad T61 has always been
flaky - sudden disconnects, especially when the signal is weak.
Supposedly Hardy will fix this, so I have been using a Netgear WG511T
borrowed from Keith instead. However, the wireless LED above the
keyboard has never come on regardless of which device I use.

There has recently been a discussion on the Thinkpad e-list that I
subscribe to about how to get the LED to work and, at the same time,
upgrade to the latest driver from Intel. I did it. The LED now works.
Yay!

And now the wireless is completely dead. 

However, I suspect there is a different problem than the driver. Some
facts:

1) The Netgear card also fails to work now. (That alone should be proof
that something else is boogered up.)

2) If I do iwlist wlan0 scan, about half the time it shows all the
networks, the rest of the time it says no networks were found. Doing
killall  NetworkManager, then restarting it, restores the scanning
ability. I can also restore it by doing modprobe -r iwl4965, then
modprobing it to restart it. But eventually iwlist scan fails again.

3) If I use kwifimanager it never sees any networks, even when iwlist
at the command line is working. If I use System > Administration >
Network, go into the Properties, gturn off roaming, and click on the
drop-down button it will display all the available networks about one
try out of 50.

4) If I do iwconfig wlan0 essid <name of network> I never fail to
connect. But that just gets me connected. I still don't have an IP
address, and nothing I have tried so far can get me an IP address.

I have concluded that my problem is that I can connect fine (although
some of the software tools seems kind of flaky), but I cannot ever get
an IP address. 

So my queries are:

1) Is there a command line tool to get an IP address from an access
point? 

2) I searched all over Ubuntu forums and failed to get a definition of
"roaming mode." Does anyone know what it is?

2) Does anyone have any other suggestions?

From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Apr  9 12:35:04 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 9 Apr 2008 12:35:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless (sigh)
In-Reply-To: <20080409121037.77d464bf.johnxj@comcast.net>

Message-ID: <c834ec80804091235q5f68f8capa40fbf7091e24ca3@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Apr 9, 2008 at 12:10 PM, John Jason Jordan <johnxj at comcast.net> wrote:
>
>  1) Is there a command line tool to get an IP address from an access
>  point?
>

$ dhclient wlan0   # or eth0, or eth1, or whatever interface you want
to get an ip for.

I think there is another dhcp implementation called dhcp-client, but
dhclient is what shows up on my ubuntu box.

Another way to tweak networking is with the boot-up scripts in /etc/init.d

# stopping your network:
$ sudo /etc/init.d/networking stop

# start up the network:
$ sudo /etc/init.d/networking start

# both in one command:
$ sudo /etc/init.d/networking restart


The /etc/init.d/networking script will use values from /etc/network/interfaces

Example interfaces file:

# Local loop-back interface:
auto lo
iface lo inet loopback

# my wifi interface (from memory... I'm not near my laptop)
auto eth1
iface eth1 inet dhcp
wireless-essid myWirelessAPid
# wireless-essid someOtherWirelessEssid

When I change APs I "just" edit the interfaces file to uncomment the
essid I want to use, commenting out all the others (I have 6-8 listed
in there) and then run the restart script.  It's annoying, but it's
good to know about for debugging.

--Rogan

On Wed, 2008-04-09 at 12:10 -0700, John Jason Jordan wrote:
> 2) Does anyone have any other suggestions? 
> 
Dear John, 

I normally connect as Rogan has suggested, configuring
the /etc/network/interfaces configuration file. It can also be
configured with static network information, available with the "man
interfaces" command. My /etc/network/interfaces looks something like:

auto lo
iface lo inet loopback

iface eth1 inet static
address 192.168.x.x
netmask 255.255.255.0
gateway 192.168.x.x
wireless-essid someid

auto eth1

That serves me well at home, where I have 3 essid's, and prefer to stay
connected to one. Of course, this assumes you understand IPv4
addressing,and know appropriate static IP addresses. If so, just be
careful to cite an address not used or assigned on your LAN.

When I connect remotely, I do as you do to connect to a remote network,
(sudo iwconfig eth1 essid someremote) and then run the 

sudo dhclient eth1

command - substitute your device name (wlan0) for eth1 (in both the
command and /etc/network/interfaces).

One other thing, I find the iwlist command finds more networks when
prefaced with the administrative sudo. It does even better if I first
"connect" the wireless card to a random essid 

sudo iwconfig eth1 essid bogus
sudo iwlist eth1 scan

Thanks,
Mike

It's a good question and/or idea.
I can possibly translate about 60 - 70% of his graphical ideas into
HTML/CSS. The rest will be complicated by HTML/CSS limitations and my 
insufficient experience in the graphical design itself.
The problem, however, is that any slight changes in the original design
would require big modifications in its corresponding HTML/CSS translations.

I can already envision a necessity for the Web designer's tool which would 
instantly translate page objects and their descriptions into corresponding HTML 
tags, forms, tables and such, and translate their positions, orientations, 
colors and other properties into corresponding CSS directives.

At the present moment creating a Web page is like creating a scientific 
publication in LaTEX in the mids of 90's.

John,
You can run "tcpdump"  on the wlan0 interface to see the interaction of
packets going back and forth between you and the AP while trying to get a
DHCP lease.

IIRC correctly when you get a valid lease it should be something like

Request
Offer
Ack
Offer
Accept

If you sniff the traffic you should be able to see if the AP is sending any
traffic at all to you. Pretty much the sniffer dump won't mean much to you
so post it here and I'll look at it and see if we can figure out whats going
on.

Drew-

It also just occurred to me that you might be getting a false association to
the AP and thats why you're not getting an IP address. Its not that the
software is flaky per se. You can configure whatever you want on the command
line and the interface will come up even if the AP isn't associating with
your laptop, I'll double check this to make sure this statement is correct
but I'm almost certain of it. Maybe googling for "unable to associate to
access point" will point you in the right direction.

I have seen an odd problem with dhcp and wireless -- and an even odder
solution.

Try the following commands as root and see if they fix the problem.

  touch /etc/dhclient.conf
  touch /etc/dhclient-wlan0.conf

When I create these two files my wireless dhcp connect problems go away. 
I have no clue why.

Tell me if that works.

On 4/10/08, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
>    Running a python application as a user I cannot redirect output of a shell
>  command to /dev/nul; apparently only root can do that.

something is probably wrong with your system if you cannot redirect
output for any application run from the shell.  however, you might
want to check that you are trying to use /dev/null rather than
/dev/nul (note the second "l").

the permissions on /dev/null should be 666.


>    I don't want to send stderr to stdout,

then you'll have to redirect them both separately.  1> /dev/null 2>
/dev/null.  why not do > /dev/null 2>&1 which has the same effect?

You should be able to do this as a normal user.  Is the "/dev/nul" typo
above just in this email, or were you not trying to write to the correct

would be restricted as a normal user since that file wouldn't exist and
only root can write new files to that directory.

From robert.citek at gmail.com  Thu Apr 10 16:11:07 2008
From: robert.citek at gmail.com (Robert Citek)
Date: Thu, 10 Apr 2008 18:11:07 -0500
Subject: [PLUG] Suppressing Screen Display of Program Output -- RESOLVED
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804101535390.4256@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804101531310.4256@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804101535390.4256@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <4145b6790804101611h6692f52ex39299d2d83ad3879@mail.gmail.com>

On Thu, Apr 10, 2008 at 5:36 PM, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
> On Thu, 10 Apr 2008, Rich Shepard wrote:
>
>  >   I don't want to send stderr to stdout, but to suppress the display when
>  > pdflatex is run in a system shell. What command do I use?
>
>    Well, '>2&' works just fine.

That doesn't sound like it will do what you describe above as that
will redirect stdout to a file called 2 in the background.  As Chris
mentioned, you probably want to do something like this:

$ { date ; zdate ; }  2> log.stderr 1> log.stdout

2 is the filedescriptor for stderr and 1 is for stdout.

Be careful with redirection as order matters.  For example, these are
not the same:

$ { date ; zdate ; }  2>&1 > /dev/null
$ { date ; zdate ; }  > /dev/null 2>&1

Although the latter command is similar to this command:

$ { date ; zdate ; } &> /dev/null

For more details, I recommend "Learning the Bash Shell":

http://books.google.com/books?id=dzBCH3x6fYEC

Regards,
- Robert

From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Fri Apr 11 07:19:58 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 07:19:58 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] more buffering than i'd like
In-Reply-To: <86lk3kodnr.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86lk3kodnr.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <20080411141958.GA2535@sentinelchicken.org>

Hello Russell,

On Fri, Apr 11, 2008 at 04:04:56AM -0700, Russell Senior wrote:
> 
> I have a program, called sample, that logs data to a file using stdout
> redirection:
> 
>   $ sample > output.data
> 
> When I check on the output.data file, e.g. with tail -f:
> 
>   $ tail -f output.data
> 
> not unexpectedly, I get blocky output as the redirect is being
> buffered somewhere or other.  This is all familiar, but ... I'd like
> to make it not be buffered (that is, I want the lines to show up as
> the come out of "sample") and I vaguely remember making something like
> that happen in the Before Time.  Unfortunately, that's about all I
> remember.  Anyone kind enough to supply me a refresher?

If your program is written in C, you could try using fflush(3) or
fsync(2) to clear the buffer after each line or other logical data chunk
is written.

If your program is a Python script, then try sys.stdout.flush().

HTH,
tim

From robert.citek at gmail.com  Fri Apr 11 08:54:23 2008
From: robert.citek at gmail.com (Robert Citek)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 10:54:23 -0500
Subject: [PLUG] more buffering than i'd like
In-Reply-To: <86lk3kodnr.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86lk3kodnr.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <4145b6790804110854i5e4a5034w708c4bf12dcaa6ca@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Apr 11, 2008 at 6:04 AM, Russell Senior <seniorr at aracnet.com> wrote:
>  When I check on the output.data file, e.g. with tail -f:
>
>   $ tail -f output.data

Use -s.  The default is 1.0 seconds.  Decrease that.  For example,
contrast this:

$ true && {
for i in {1..100} ; do echo $i ; sleep 0.1 ; done > output.txt &
tail -f output.txt
}

with this:

$ true && {
for i in {1..100} ; do echo $i ; sleep 0.1 ; done > output.txt &
tail -s 0.2 -f output.txt
}

Regards,
- Robert

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Fri Apr 11 11:19:04 2008
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 11:19:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] best tool to convert a bitfield structure to #define?
Message-ID: <47FFAB98.20901@seitzassoc.com>

I need to convert a bunch of structures with bitfields to #defines. 
The structures describe hardware registers that I need to access via 
assembly code.  What tool would you use to do this, awk, perl, python, 
or something else?


This:
struct ADCTRL1_BITS {     // bits  description
     Uint16  rsvd1:4;      // 3:0   reserved
     Uint16  SEQ_CASC:1;   // 4     Cascaded sequencer mode
     Uint16  SEQ_OVRD:1;   // 5     Sequencer override
     Uint16  CONT_RUN:1;   // 6     Continuous run
     Uint16  CPS:1;        // 7     ADC core clock pre-scalar
     Uint16  ACQ_PS:4;     // 11:8  Acquisition window size
     Uint16  SUSMOD:2;     // 13:12 Emulation suspend mode
     Uint16  RESET:1;      // 14    ADC reset
     Uint16  rsvd2:1;      // 15    reserved
};

needs to be converted to this:
#define ADCTRL1_SEQ_CASC  0x0010
#define ADCTRL1_SEQ_OVRD  0x0020
#define ADCTRL1_CONT_RUN  0x0040
#define ADCTRL1_CPS       0x0080
#define ADCTRL1_ACQ_PS    0x0100
#define ADCTRL1_SUSMOD    0x1000
#define ADCTRL1_RESET     0x4000

or perhaps this:
#define ADCTRL1_SEQ_CASC  4
#define ADCTRL1_SEQ_OVRD  5
#define ADCTRL1_CONT_RUN  6
#define ADCTRL1_CPS       7
#define ADCTRL1_ACQ_PS    8
#define ADCTRL1_SUSMOD    12
#define ADCTRL1_RESET     14

BTW, using information contained in the comments is not allowed, as 
the comments are not guaranteed to be correct.

thanks,
galen

From raanders at acm.org  Fri Apr 11 12:47:22 2008
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 12:47:22 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] IMAP: Using and Administration
Message-ID: <47FFC04A.5030108@acm.org>

Anyone know of a good article, paper or book on IMAP.  Not just how to 
set it up on a server or how to configure a mail client to use IMAP but 
somethnig explains the really neat features and how to use them.

Some I'm kind-of aware of are: shared folders (well actually mailboxes 
in IMAP terms), server administrators that can create/modify users and 
access their mailboxes/folders without having their password.

I've seen references to these capabilities in reading the RFCs and 
looking at modules on CPAN.

I think some of this is tied to how the IMAP server (software) is built.

I am creating an application that needs to inventory a users IMAP 
mailboxes and create a report for them.  Fortunately the software I'm 
writing this for stores users passwords in plain text in a database I 
have access to but that may go away in a future version.


Thanks for any pointers of ideas,
Rod

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Fri Apr 11 14:47:39 2008
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 14:47:39 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] IMAP: Using and Administration
In-Reply-To: <47FFC04A.5030108@acm.org>
References: <47FFC04A.5030108@acm.org>
Message-ID: <1207950459.32706.29.camel@welkins.pdx.odshp.com>


On Fri, 2008-04-11 at 12:47 -0700, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:
> Anyone know of a good article, paper or book on IMAP.  Not just how to 
> set it up on a server or how to configure a mail client to use IMAP but 
> somethnig explains the really neat features and how to use them.
> 
> Some I'm kind-of aware of are: shared folders (well actually mailboxes 
> in IMAP terms), server administrators that can create/modify users and 
> access their mailboxes/folders without having their password.

There's an old O'Reilly book about it. The chapters on Cyrus are old.
Reading the cyrus-users list and documentation helps, as does reading
the RFCs, which I needed to do for some of my scripts.

> I've seen references to these capabilities in reading the RFCs and 
> looking at modules on CPAN.
> 
> I think some of this is tied to how the IMAP server (software) is built.

Indeed. There is a variety of optional IMAP features and not every
client and server implements all of them.

> I am creating an application that needs to inventory a users IMAP 
> mailboxes and create a report for them.  Fortunately the software I'm 
> writing this for stores users passwords in plain text in a database I 
> have access to but that may go away in a future version.

You might find some examples in the couple of little scripts that I've
written:

http://haus.nakedape.cc/svn/public/trunk/small-projects/mail-utils/

Are you looking for a way around having to store the user's passwords?
You can use proxy authentication, where you authenticate as an
administrator and be authorized as a user. The IMAP server
implementation needs to support it; Cyrus does, I know. I have not
actually used it, however.



From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Fri Apr 11 14:56:48 2008
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 14:56:48 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless (sigh)
In-Reply-To: <20080409121037.77d464bf.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <20080409121037.77d464bf.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <1207951008.32706.32.camel@welkins.pdx.odshp.com>


On Wed, 2008-04-09 at 12:10 -0700, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> I have concluded that my problem is that I can connect fine (although
> some of the software tools seems kind of flaky), but I cannot ever get
> an IP address. 

I don't suppose there is any chance the firewall has been turned on, is
there?

Run 'iptables -nvL' as root to list. If your firewall is disabled, it
should look like:

Chain INPUT (policy ACCEPT 0 packets, 0 bytes)
 pkts bytes target     prot opt in     out     source               destination         

Chain FORWARD (policy ACCEPT 0 packets, 0 bytes)
 pkts bytes target     prot opt in     out     source               destination         

Chain OUTPUT (policy ACCEPT 0 packets, 0 bytes)
 pkts bytes target     prot opt in     out     source               destination 

Wil

PLUG Advanced Topics Meeting
April 16th, 2008  7-9pm

Jax Bar
826 SW 2nd Avenue
Portland, Oregon

Speaker:  Selena Deckelmann <selenamarie at gmail.com>

Topic: PostgreSQL monitoring

Ever wanted a command-line tool for monitoring PostgreSQL? ptop is the
answer! Derived from the UNIX utility top, ptop automates some of the
most common troubleshooting queries. This talk will provide an
introduction to PostgreSQL monitoring, supported features in ptop, and
plans for future development.

Features include:

    * List of currently running queries
    * Viewing query plans
    * Viewing locks
    * View current user table and index statistics
    * Deltas on statistics at configurable intervals

Development is active, and the tool is currently supported on *BSD and
Linux, with a Mac OS X port on the way.

The project's home page is at:
http://pgfoundry.org/projects/ptop
Biography:

Selena Deckelmann bikes herself to work everyday at Chris King
Precision Components, a bicycle parts manufacturer in Portland, OR,
where she is Information Systems Manager. She is User Group Liaison
for the PostgreSQL Global Development Group. She currently leads
PDXPUG - http://pugs.postgresql.org/pdx, a PostgreSQL Users Group, and
is helping start a programming group, Code-n-Splode -
http://pdx.codensplode.org, whose goal is to get more women involved
in open source. In her spare time, she collects eggs from her
chickens, gardens and occasionally mixes drinks for her local Perl
Mongers group.

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Fri Apr 11 17:06:20 2008
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Fri, 11 Apr 2008 17:06:20 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] best tool to convert a bitfield structure to #define?
In-Reply-To: <47FFB6BC.5000709@fredjame.cnc.net>
References: <47FFAB98.20901@seitzassoc.com> <47FFB6BC.5000709@fredjame.cnc.net>
Message-ID: <47FFFCFC.60506@seitzassoc.com>

Fred James wrote:
> Galen Seitz wrote:
> 
>> I need to convert a bunch of structures with bitfields to #defines. 
>> The structures describe hardware registers that I need to access via 
>> assembly code.  What tool would you use to do this, awk, perl, python, 
>> or something else?
>>
>>
>> This:
>> struct ADCTRL1_BITS {     // bits  description
>>     Uint16  rsvd1:4;      // 3:0   reserved
>>     Uint16  SEQ_CASC:1;   // 4     Cascaded sequencer mode
>>     Uint16  SEQ_OVRD:1;   // 5     Sequencer override
>>     Uint16  CONT_RUN:1;   // 6     Continuous run
>>     Uint16  CPS:1;        // 7     ADC core clock pre-scalar
>>     Uint16  ACQ_PS:4;     // 11:8  Acquisition window size
>>     Uint16  SUSMOD:2;     // 13:12 Emulation suspend mode
>>     Uint16  RESET:1;      // 14    ADC reset
>>     Uint16  rsvd2:1;      // 15    reserved
>> };
>>
>> needs to be converted to this:
>> #define ADCTRL1_SEQ_CASC  0x0010
>> #define ADCTRL1_SEQ_OVRD  0x0020
>> #define ADCTRL1_CONT_RUN  0x0040
>> #define ADCTRL1_CPS       0x0080
>> #define ADCTRL1_ACQ_PS    0x0100
>> #define ADCTRL1_SUSMOD    0x1000
>> #define ADCTRL1_RESET     0x4000
>>
>> or perhaps this:
>> #define ADCTRL1_SEQ_CASC  4
>> #define ADCTRL1_SEQ_OVRD  5
>> #define ADCTRL1_CONT_RUN  6
>> #define ADCTRL1_CPS       7
>> #define ADCTRL1_ACQ_PS    8
>> #define ADCTRL1_SUSMOD    12
>> #define ADCTRL1_RESET     14
>>
>> BTW, using information contained in the comments is not allowed, as 
>> the comments are not guaranteed to be correct.
>>
>> thanks,
>> galen
>>
>>  
>>
> Galen Seitz
> The second example should be easy enough with SED, but either shouldn't 
> be too difficult with AWK ... I am basing that reply on the observation 
> that the lines of interest have a common address pattern "Uint16", 
> followed by the field of interest, which is in turn two fields separated 
> by a colon.  Hope this helps, or have I missed something?
> Regards
> Fred James

Thanks for the suggestion.  I ended up grabbing my Camel book and 
cobbling together the following:

#!/usr/bin/perl

while ($line = <>) {
     next if (!($line =~ /^struct\s+\w+_BITS\s*/));
     ($register) = ($line =~ /^struct\s+(\w+)_BITS\s*/);
     $position = 0;
     while ($line = <>) {
	last if ($line =~ /}\s*;/);
         ($field, $size) = ($line =~ /\s+(\w+):(\d+);/);
         print ("#define ${register}_$field $position\n") if (!($field 
=~ /rsvd\d*/));
         $position += $size;
     }
}

I'm sure it's not great Perl, but it does seem to work.

galen

From sjansen at buscaluz.org  Sat Apr 12 09:12:33 2008
From: sjansen at buscaluz.org (Stuart Jansen)
Date: Sat, 12 Apr 2008 10:12:33 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] find | while read
Message-ID: <1208016753.7119.22.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>

Ever since I was taught "while read" as a method to avoid whitespace
problems, it has been one of my favorite shell scripting tricks.
Unfortunately, while working on a git script yesterday, I discovered an
instance where it doesn't work. Specifically, Bash is leaking the output
of find to the screen and horking stdin.

I found a workaround, but it's more complex than I like. I've included
three generations of a simplified script as an example. What I'd like to
know is, does anyone know a more sane method for looping over a list of
files produced by a command like find, git or anything else?

NOTE: To save time, let me point out that git doesn't have an equivalent
of find's --exec, so that's out. In addition, the script has to handle
whitespace in filenames so "for FILE in $( ... )" is also out. I have a
sneaking suspicion that changing $IFS could lead to a solution, but the
mere idea freaks me out.

Any takers?

# ==================================
# Simple but doesn't work
# ==================================
find . -name '*.txt' | \
while read FILE
do
    echo Spell checking $FILE
    aspell -c "$FILE"
done
# ==================================


# ==================================
# Insane but works
# ==================================
TEMP=$(mktemp)
exec 3<>"$TEMP"
find . -name '*.txt' > "$TEMP"
while read FILE <&3
do 
    echo Spell checking $FILE
    aspell -c "$FILE"
done
exec 3>&-
rm "$TEMP"
# ==================================


# ==================================
# Insane but works and more secure
# ==================================
TEMP=$(mktemp)
exec 3<>"$TEMP"
find . -name '*.txt' > "$TEMP"
while read FILE <&3
do 
(
    exec 3>&- # Avoid leaking the FD
    echo Spell checking $FILE
    aspell -c "$FILE"
)
done
exec 3>&-
rm "$TEMP"
# ==================================




From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Sat Apr 12 09:58:19 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Sat, 12 Apr 2008 09:58:19 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] find | while read
In-Reply-To: <1208016753.7119.22.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>
References: <1208016753.7119.22.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>
Message-ID: <20080412165819.GA12973@sentinelchicken.org>


> I found a workaround, but it's more complex than I like. I've included
> three generations of a simplified script as an example. What I'd like to
> know is, does anyone know a more sane method for looping over a list of
> files produced by a command like find, git or anything else?


I'm not intimately familiar with what you've got going, but often I rely
on the combination of find and xargs with NUL termination.  The only
characters not allowed in a file name in UNIX are '\0' and '/'.  If the
file names are NUL terminated, then you don't have to worry about nasty
parsing issues.  Unfortunately not too many tools support parsing based
on this, but xargs does:

  find . -name '*.txt' -print0 | xargs -0 aspell -c

To do multiple commands at once for a single file, you'd probably need
to muck around with the -I option in xargs.

good luck,
tim

Date: Sat, 12 Apr 2008 12:03:49 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] better spam filtering through google
Message-ID: <18432.63877.127511.299809@localhost.localdomain>

I had a major spam problem on my hands.  Even with a mail setup that
includes amavisd and spamasassin, tons of spam was getting through.

Then I stumbled across
dev-perl/Mail-SpamAssassin-Plugin-GoogleSafeBrowsing (at least this is
what it is called in the gentoo portage tree).  The URL to it is
http://search.cpan.org/search?query=Mail-SpamAssassin-Plugin-GoogleSafeBrowsing&mode=dist

I've only been running it for a week, but this spamasassin module has
been working with a 100% success rate.  There must be over 500 spams
in my quarantine thanks to it, but no false positives whatsoever.

I also installed mail-filter/spamassassin-botnet
( http://people.ucsc.edu/~jrudd/spamassassin/ ), which also has
contributed to higher spam scores.  I think the problem I had was that
spams were being identified, but not generating high enough scores to
reach the threshold.  More filters = higher scores.

Carlos Konstanski

Well, keep in mind that file names can contain new lines.  Unlikely to
happen in normal situations, but if someone wanted to sabotage your
script, they could easily create one.  The output from git in this case
would probably be hopelessly ambiguous.

Please pardon the security paranoia... =)

Subject: [PLUG] automounting a dm-crypt based filesystem on a fixed device
Message-ID: <48013277.4070400@seitzassoc.com>

I would like to automount a dm-crypt based filesystem that is located 
on a fixed device.  The idea here is for both my wife and myself to 
have access to a shared directory structure that contains sensitive 
data(tax returns, etc.).  I don't want the filesystem or dm-crypt 
device to always be active, as most of the time it is not needed.  I'd 
like access to be demand-based.  Does anyone know how to do this? 
There are lots of instructions on the net for doing this with 
removable devices, but I haven't found any that would apply to a fixed 
device.

If there is a way to have autofs trigger hal, it might be possible to 
warp the following to my needs.
   http://www.flyn.org/easycrypto/easycrypto.html

It might look something like this:
   autofs calls hal
   hal calls gnome volumer manager
   gnome volume manager asks user for passphrase
   gnome volume manager hands passphrase to hal
   hal calls cryptsetup
   autofs mounts dm-crypt device
   filesystem available
   autofs idle timeout expires
   autofs umounts dm-crypt device
   autofs calls hal
   hal performs cryptsetup close

Thoughts?

thanks,
galen

Yes, I am running postfix, and this is server-side filtering.  But I
think the google module would work equally well with a client-side
spamasassin implementation.  By the time the google plugin gets to see
the email, we're well within the spamasassin process, and it shoudn't
matter how we got there.  The same blacklist is used by google for
their firefox plugin for detecting phishing sites.

I guess I like the idea that I can so easily take advantage of all
that hard work google does to maintain its blacklist.  This has the
potential for making a homebrewed linux mail server as spam-free as
any corporate lunker.  Where I work we route all our mail through
Postini (an expensive corporate offsite solution), yet some of us
still get all kinds of obvious, easily filterable spam (you can
imagine some of the keywords these emails contain).  I have to wonder
if our vendors (like Oracle) are selling our email addresses!

Carlos Konstanski


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Apr 12 17:41:36 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 12 Apr 2008 17:41:36 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] better spam filtering through google
In-Reply-To: <18432.63877.127511.299809@localhost.localdomain>
References: <18432.63877.127511.299809@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <20080413004136.GA30447@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Sat, Apr 12, 2008 at 12:03:49PM -0600, Carlos Konstanski wrote:
...
> http://search.cpan.org/search?query=Mail-SpamAssassin-Plugin-GoogleSafeBrowsing&mode=dist
...

Looks interesting.  I just installed it, to see if it works.

The instructions on the page are a little wonky.

I had to install the module  "Net::Google::SafeBrowsing::Blocklist" 
by downloading the tar.gz file through the webpage, untarring it,
then doing the usual "perl Makefile.PL"  followed by  "make install"
(as root).  Then I could install the other two modules with "cpan -i"

The page suggests installing a cron job that runs every 25 minutes.
That is a little difficult to describe in /etc/crontab .  I made the
script ( which I called spamgoogle) run every 15 minutes with the
crontab entry:

   05,20,35,50 * * * * root /usr/local/sbin/spamgoogle > /dev/null

At the bottom of the page, there are 7 lines to be added to 
/etc/mail/spamassassin/local.cf .  These are all supposed to be
in the box, but some typos goofed up the first three lines.

I'm eagerly anticipating the absence of spam, and the continued 
presence of the mail I want.  I am combining this with greylisting
at my outside facing server (which catches one spam attempt every
2 seconds) so hopefully this will turn the recent 30 spams per day
into one or less per day.

Keith

output produced by an arbitrary program and assigned each line to a
variable. Any solution must be able to handle output containing
whitespace without corrupting it. I would also prefer to be able to call
functions instead of resorting to helper scripts.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Sat Apr 12 23:11:11 2008
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Sat, 12 Apr 2008 23:11:11 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] find | while read
In-Reply-To: <1208016753.7119.22.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>
References: <1208016753.7119.22.camel@simplicity.buscaluz.org>
Message-ID: <200804122311.11243.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Stuart Jansen
# on Saturday 12 April 2008 09:12:

>find . -name '*.txt' | \
>while read FILE
>do
>? ? echo Spell checking $FILE
>? ? aspell -c "$FILE"
>done

Right.  You can't have your stdin and have your stdin too.

  $ echo 'a
  b
  o q' | while read FILE; do perl -e 'while(my $line = <STDIN>) {
    warn "I ate your $line"}'; done
  I ate your b
  I ate your o q

So, if your loop command expects STDIN to be a TTY, xargs -d '\n' -n 1 
won't help either unless you want to find a way to stick a terminal 
between the xargs and the command:

  find . -name '*.txt' | xargs -d '\n' -n 1 xterm -e  aspell -c

Alternatively, you could do it in perl with the find (git) command as a 
piped open fork, thus the parent process still has a STDIN to lend to 
the aspell.

  perl -e '
  open(my $fh, "-|", qw(find . -name *.txt));
  while(my $file = <$fh>) {
    chomp($file);
    system(qw(aspell -c), $file) and die "ouch";
  }
  '

--Eric
-- 
Minimum wage help gives you minimum service.
--David Schomer

    http://scratchcomputing.com

I've done it in trivial scripts and small inner loops, but because its a
pretty low-level setting and I don't yet fully understand the effects of
changing it, I tend to fear it. Instinct tells me that modifying $IFS in
anything other than trivial scripts is just asking for trouble, but
maybe that isn't true if you know how to manage the consequences.

Have you written any non-trival scripts that modify $IFS? Are you
familiar with the side effects of changing it, and can you give advice
on how to control them?

anything which is likely to choke until you leave the scope under which 
the local is in effect.  That's just based on my knowledge of perl and 
reading of `help local`, but the general theme is the same everywhere:  
when you modify a magic global which effects the core of the 
interpreter, you either use your language's scoping tools to restrict 
the range of influence or you put it back where you found it when 
you're done.

Thus, we have perl idioms like the following, and often see $|, $_, and 
various "knobs" from `perldoc perlvar` used with local().

  my $string = do { open(my $fh, '<', $file) or die; local $/; <$fh>};

--Eric
-- 
Like a lot of people, I was mathematically abused as a child.
--Paul Graham

From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Sun Apr 13 15:11:59 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Sun, 13 Apr 2008 15:11:59 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] What's Wrong With This IP Address?
In-Reply-To: <48026B3E.2030105@fredjame.cnc.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804131008180.29366@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<480248CA.70902@fredjame.cnc.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804131057380.29366@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<48026B3E.2030105@fredjame.cnc.net>
Message-ID: <20080413221159.GD28997@sentinelchicken.org>

> But to 
> the question "If a direct connection can be made with a spoofed IP 
> address ..." - this is email we are talking about, yes?  (a) It isn't 
> new, and (b) it is possible the IP has no relationship to the actual 
> point of origin.


Well... Here's my take on it.  The big question is: who added that
Received header?  Any number of forged Received headers are trivial to
add before the spammer sends it on to it's destination or relay, but
once it is out of her control, the Received headers are usually
relatively trustworthy.  The big question is, what is the first
trustworthy Received header?  Remember these are stamped in a stack of
sorts, with the oldest toward the bottom.

Assuming you can trust the Received header (i.e. the server that stamped
it is trustworthy), then the likelihood of a spammer spoofing a TCP/SMTP
converstaion is likely very low.  Provided you're using an even remotely
recent operating system, then you should have mostly unpredictable TCP
sequence numbers and an attacker would generally need to guess these in
the right order to keep the conversation alive long enough to complete
the transaction*.

Hope that answers your question on spoofing,
tim


* There are exceptions to this.  If the target mail server honors loose
  source routing, an attacker could spoof the source address while
  embedding her real address in the list of routers.  It is my
  impression that few, if any, hosts will allow this and certainly
  firewalls generally block these headers.  Within a local network
  these attacks are often still possible though.

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Mon Apr 14 11:45:56 2008
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Mon, 14 Apr 2008 11:45:56 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] simple grep/regex question
Message-ID: <4803A664.1070407@seitzassoc.com>

I'd like to match all occurrences of a given word that are not 
preceded at any point by a particular character.  Specifically, I want 
to match all occurrences of the word 'bit' that are not in an assembly 
language comment, where the comment character is ';'.  For example, I 
want to match the second line, but not the first.

       sacl mode,2   ; set mode bit2=1 to SCS
       bit my_settings,bit11   ; am I articulated?

I've tried these:
  grep '[^;]*bit' foo.asm   # matches all bit
  grep '[^;]+bit' foo.asm   # matches nothing


Thanks for your help.

galen



From jeme at brelin.net  Mon Apr 14 11:54:26 2008
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)
Date: Mon, 14 Apr 2008 13:54:26 -0500 (CDT)
Subject: [PLUG] simple grep/regex question
In-Reply-To: <4803A664.1070407@seitzassoc.com>
References: <4803A664.1070407@seitzassoc.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804141351320.11158@shadow.bitmine.net>


On Mon, 14 Apr 2008, Galen Seitz wrote:
> I've tried these:
>  grep '[^;]*bit' foo.asm   # matches all bit

That's because the "bit" is preceeded by one or more non-; characters.

Make sure you match the start of the line in your regex and you're good:

grep "^[^;]*bit" foo.asm  # matches what you need!

J.

From robert.citek at gmail.com  Mon Apr 14 12:14:02 2008
From: robert.citek at gmail.com (Robert Citek)
Date: Mon, 14 Apr 2008 14:14:02 -0500
Subject: [PLUG] simple grep/regex question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0804141351320.11158@shadow.bitmine.net>
References: <4803A664.1070407@seitzassoc.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0804141351320.11158@shadow.bitmine.net>
Message-ID: <4145b6790804141214o5fb06b2aof1f07e10d97d0386@mail.gmail.com>

On Mon, Apr 14, 2008 at 1:54 PM, Jeme A Brelin <jeme at brelin.net> wrote:
>  On Mon, 14 Apr 2008, Galen Seitz wrote:
>  > I've tried these:
>  >  grep '[^;]*bit' foo.asm   # matches all bit
>
>  That's because the "bit" is preceeded by one or more non-; characters.
>
>  Make sure you match the start of the line in your regex and you're good:
>
>  grep "^[^;]*bit" foo.asm  # matches what you need!

A little trick I like to use to help me design REs is to add the
--color option to grep:

$ grep --color '[^;]*bit' foo.asm
$ grep --color '[^;]+bit' foo.asm
$ grep --color "^[^;]*bit" foo.asm

The --color option shows me the pattern that matched.  If I want
context, I'll use one of the -A, -B, or -C option, or I'll tack on an
extra expression -e ^.  For example:

$ grep -C 100 --color "^[^;]*bit" foo.asm
$ grep --color -e "^[^;]*bit"  -e ^ foo.asm

And if there's a lot of data, I'll adjust --color and pipe the output into less:

$ grep --color=always -e "^[^;]*bit"  -e ^ foo.asm | less -r

Good luck and let us know how things go.

Regards,
- Robert

From andi598d at gmail.com  Mon Apr 14 14:11:30 2008
From: andi598d at gmail.com (Andreas Turriff)
Date: Mon, 14 Apr 2008 14:11:30 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Postfix mystery...
In-Reply-To: <1208207246.27057.5.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
References: <1208207246.27057.5.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <8bbd30b30804141411w3755d535wfffe0a8dcbb7d77@mail.gmail.com>

Postfix documentation points to this function:

*smtpd_reject_unlisted_recipient (default: yes)*

Request that the Postfix SMTP server rejects mail for unknown recipient
addresses, even when no explicit
reject_unlisted_recipient<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#reject_unlisted_recipient>access
restriction is specified. This prevents the Postfix queue from
filling up with undeliverable MAILER-DAEMON messages.

   - The recipient domain matches
$mydestination<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#mydestination>,
   $inet_interfaces<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#inet_interfaces>or $
   proxy_interfaces<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#proxy_interfaces>,
   but the recipient is not listed in
$local_recipient_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#local_recipient_maps>,
   and $local_recipient_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#local_recipient_maps>is
not null.
   - The recipient domain matches
$virtual_alias_domains<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#virtual_alias_domains>but
the recipient is not listed in $
   virtual_alias_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#virtual_alias_maps>.

   - The recipient domain matches
$virtual_mailbox_domains<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#virtual_mailbox_domains>but
the recipient is not listed in $
   virtual_mailbox_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#virtual_mailbox_maps>,
   and $virtual_mailbox_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#virtual_mailbox_maps>is
not null.
   - The recipient domain matches
$relay_domains<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#relay_domains>but
the recipient is not listed in $
   relay_recipient_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#relay_recipient_maps>,
   and $relay_recipient_maps<http://www.postfix.org/postconf.5.html#relay_recipient_maps>is
not null.

 This feature is available in Postfix 2.1 and later.

>From www.postfix.org.

Hope this helps,

~Andreas
